<body class="c120 doc-content">
    <p class="c74 c19 c18 title" id="h.jae1x5jpy6fo"><span class="c71 c10">Page Design for storing Played Games for
            Reversi/Othello with efficient navigation queries</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_pq6wkhvlrwav-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Anmol Agarwal (2019101068), Sanchit Arora (2019101047)</span>
        </li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c10 c73">Game rules</span><span class="c10">: </span><span class="c3 c85"><a class="c75"
                href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reversi&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1671217651750446&amp;usg=AOvVaw0nXiUt3QXFM4mPGn9QfIss">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reversi</a></span><span
            class="c12">&nbsp;</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10">Some rules</span><span>&nbsp;</span><span
            class="c10">&amp;</span><span>&nbsp;</span><span class="c10">board invariants</span><span>&nbsp;</span><span
            class="c21 c10">worth highlighting for the purpose of our design:</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_qb73tru7a1sd-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10">A1:</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;Different sources mention
                different criteria for ending of the game when a player cannot move. Some sources say that the game ends
                when either player cannot move. Others say that the game ends only when BOTH players are not able to
                move.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_qb73tru7a1sd-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span>We assume: </span><span class="c65">GAME ENDS when even one player does not
                have a move left</span><span class="c12">.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_qb73tru7a1sd-0">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10">A2:</span><span>&nbsp;The disks on the board make </span><span
                class="c10">ONE SINGLE connected component</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;(where valid moves are
                horizontal, vertical and diagonal). This is easy to see as a disk can be added only when at least one of
                the opponent&rsquo;s disks swaps its color.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10">A3:</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;In each move, exactly one disk
                is added to the board i.e. the number of disks on the board is the same as the number of moves done on
                the board so far.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c21 c10">Some terminology/notation:</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_ytckfz9pd0kx-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10">N</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;= side of the board =&gt; N x N
                = number of cells on the board | N&lt;=1e3</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c65">For ease of reference, without loss of generality, we consider
                the initial configuration of the board played i.e. having 4 disks as the first four moves</span><span
                class="c12">. Hence, MAX MOVES in our case: N x N (since we are considering the initial configuration of
                the game to consume 4 moves)</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10">G</span><span class="c12">: game ID</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10">TotMoves:</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;total number of moves
                played in the game.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10 c29">M</span><span class="c10 c29 c15">i</span><span
                class="c12">: ith move of the game where 1&lt;=i&lt;=TotMoves. (NOTE: M1, M2, M3 and M4 are fixed since
                they correspond to the initial configuration of the game)</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10">S</span><span class="c10 c15">i</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;=
                state of the board after Move &ldquo;i&rdquo;</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <h2 class="c6" id="h.gap4uxf7u9p4"><span class="c10 c62">Queries we are prioritizing:</span></h2>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c12">There were many page designs in our minds which could have been optimized for
            different queries for the game. While presenting our below design, we consider the below to be our topmost
            priority:</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_4m2yfy5gcus3-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Q1: Size needed to store each game</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span>Q2: Time needed to move from state </span><span class="c10">&ldquo;i&rdquo;
            </span><span>of the game to state </span><span class="c10">&ldquo;i+1&rdquo;</span><span
                class="c12">&nbsp;ie replay the game</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Q3: Time needed to quickly switch among far away states of the
                game.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_4m2yfy5gcus3-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span>Eg: instead of starting from state 1, the user can directly ask to view the
                state of the game after 4500 moves. After that, he/she can ask to </span><span
                class="c10">directly</span><span>&nbsp;move to the state of the game after move 11005 without
                transitioning through all the states from </span><span class="c10">move 4500 to 11004</span><span
                class="c12">.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <h3 class="c24 c19 c18" id="h.cp9fc7vg9kez"><span>H</span><span>ow a state change might be implemented in a OTHELLO
            GAME:</span></h3>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_1isceivp76ak-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c38">LET US ASSUME ONLY for an instant (and NOT for the remaining
                part of this document)</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;that we are able to load the entire game into
                memory into a matrix ARR where ARR[i][j] is:</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_1isceivp76ak-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">2 if cell is empty</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">0 if cell is filled by BLACK DISK</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">1 if cell is filled by WHITE DISK</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_1isceivp76ak-0">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Let&rsquo;s say a move has been made which places a white disk
                at cell (P,Q) of the board. This move can evoke a series of cascading color swaps in all 6
                directions:</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_1isceivp76ak-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Up</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Down</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Left</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Right</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Diagonal</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Reverse Diagonal</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_1isceivp76ak-0">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">As a result, due to this move, we will have to make changes in
                the matrix.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span>Since we have 6 directions to search for, in a naive implementation, we
                might have to take ATMAX &ldquo;N&rdquo; steps in each direction to
                sw</span><span>ap</span><span>&nbsp;the disk colors. So, the time complexity of making updates due to a
                move in a naive way is 6N operations approx which is </span><span class="c21 c10">O(N)</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span>Such an </span><span class="c10">O(N) update per move</span><span>&nbsp;may
                be </span><span class="c107">too inefficient for queries of type Q3</span><span>&nbsp;where the USER
                jumps between states of the game. Eg: if board size N = 1000 and the user wants to jump from move 1 to
                move 1e5, then the number of operations will be ~ 1e5 x N ~ </span><span
                class="c10">1e8</span><span>&nbsp;</span><span class="c10">operations</span><span
                class="c12">&nbsp;which is very large. To make answering such queries more efficient, we propose storing
                multiple snapshots of the game in the manner proposed later.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <h3 class="c24 c19 c18" id="h.9pomtb1dv1d6"><span class="c92 c10 c87 c29">Page Designs:</span></h3>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>While brainstorming, in our shortlisted page designs, we often found a</span><span
            class="c86">&nbsp;tradeoff between storage space needed and time needed</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;to
            update the state of the board when a move is made. As a result, in our pipeline, we try to incorporate the
            best of both worlds:</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_do4gnukzmk8w-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10">Page Design 1 (Storage based Page):</span><span>&nbsp;This is
                the design we follow to store a game. Once written, these pages are </span><span
                class="c3">READ-ONLY</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;in nature. </span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10">Page Design 2 (Update based page):</span><span>&nbsp;This page
                design is used to store the current snapshot of the game. Once the user has finished investigating the
                game, the </span><span class="c3">space occupied by these pages can be relinquished</span><span
                class="c12">. These pages are regularly updated as the user navigates through the game.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_do4gnukzmk8w-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">If the user is currently at state &ldquo;i&rdquo;, these pages
                are used to store state &ldquo;i&rdquo; of the game.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span>When the user moves to state &ldquo;i+1&rdquo; from state &ldquo;i&rdquo;,
                then updates are made within these pages themselves.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 c17 li-bullet-0"><span class="c62 c10"></span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <h2 class="c6" id="h.b680bnpkuwqd"><span>Making navigation queries efficient by using SQUARE-root decomposition type
            logic</span><span class="c10 c81">Proposal:</span></h2>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>Let us assume that game &ldquo;G&rdquo; has &ldquo;TotMoves&rdquo; total moves. Then, we
            store the snapshot (checkpoint) of the board (</span><span class="c38">using page design 1</span><span
            class="c12">) for every Kth state where K = sqrt(TotMoves).</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10">For eg:</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c32">Consider the initial empty board to be S</span><span
            class="c15 c32">0</span><span class="c23">.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c32">After move 1, the state of board transitions from S</span><span
            class="c32 c15">0 </span><span class="c32">to S</span><span class="c37 c32 c15">1.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c32">After move 2, the state of board transitions from S</span><span
            class="c32 c15">1 </span><span class="c32">to S</span><span class="c32 c15 c37">2.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c23">.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c23">.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c23">.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c32">After &ldquo;TotMoves&rdquo;, the state of the board transitions from
            S</span><span class="c32 c15">TotMoves-1 </span><span class="c32">to S</span><span
            class="c32 c15">TotMoves.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c23"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c23"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c23">Then we will be taking a snapshot after every K moves where K =
            sqrt(TotMoves).</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10 c32">Number of snapshots we will be taking will be</span><span class="c32">:
            TotMoves/K = TotMoves/sqrt(TotMoves) = sqrt(TotMoves).</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c21 c10">How does this help in answering queries efficiently ?</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_2zxn8e7whh21-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Let us consider a game with TotMoves = 1e6.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Let&rsquo;s say that a user is currently viewing state P of the
                game. Next, the user suddenly wants to move to state &ldquo;Q&rdquo; of the game. </span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10">In case we hadn&rsquo;t stored checkpoints</span><span
                class="c12">, we would have to move &ldquo;diff = Q-P&rdquo; moves ahead with O(N) operations per
                move.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_2zxn8e7whh21-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span>As a result, we would be making approx O(diff x N) operations. In the worst
                case, diff can be nearly N^2 and hence, we might end up making </span><span class="c10 c97">N^3
                operations</span><span class="c12">.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_2zxn8e7whh21-0">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10">Since we are storing checkpoints</span><span class="c12">, we
                can do the following to reach state &ldquo;Q&rdquo;:</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_2zxn8e7whh21-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Find the nearest previous checkpoint to state &ldquo;Q&rdquo;
                &nbsp;which has been stored. Let&rsquo;s call this checkpoint &ldquo;X&rdquo;.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Then, we already know the configuration of the board after move
                &ldquo;X&rdquo; (since we stored it) and hence, we now need to make only &ldquo;diff = Q-X&rdquo;
                moves.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Here, since we store a checkpoint every sqrt(TotMoves), diff
                can be atmax sqrt(TotMoves).</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span>&nbsp;In the worst case, diff can be nearly N^2 and hence, we might end up
                making (N x sqrt(TotMoves)) operations where TotMoves can be atmax N^2 and so, in worst case, we would
                end up making</span><span class="c97">&nbsp;</span><span class="c10 c97">N^2
                operations</span><span>&nbsp;</span><span class="c42">which is an improvement by a factor of
                &ldquo;N&rdquo;</span><span>&nbsp;(ie a</span><span>n improvement by a </span><span class="c38">factor
                of 1000</span><span>&nbsp;potentially for large board sized games).</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <h2 class="c117 c19 c18" id="h.6qfbehf0voev"><span class="c10 c87 c58 c104">Page Design 1 (Storage based
            Page)</span></h2>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">We propose to use this page design for storing the checkpoints of the board
            state every sqrt(TotMoves) moves as described above. These pages will only be READ-ONLY in nature.</span>
    </p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c21 c10">We will be covering this section with the help of an example:</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">Consider that we need to store the following state of the 12 x 12 board:</span>
    </p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span
            style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: -0.00px -0.00px; border: 2.67px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 273.74px; height: 268.05px;"><img
                alt="" src="images/image29.png"
                style="width: 273.74px; height: 268.05px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                title=""></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <h3 class="c24 c19 c18" id="h.5vfa4ew7vor4"><span class="c95 c123">Feature 1: </span><span
            class="c93 c10 c123 c87">Truncating the board to store only the smallest rectangle which covers the entire
            connected component</span></h3>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">First we make the following claims:</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p><a id="t.aec1af8346c034c597eb05ec85c1c8dcab333012"></a><a
        id="t.0"></a>
    <table class="c44">
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c51" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c21 c10">Claim ID</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c72" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c21 c10">Claim:</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c53" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c21 c10">Reason</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c51" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">1</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c72" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">The disks on the board make ONE SINGLE connected component (where valid
                        moves are horizontal, vertical and diagonal)</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c53" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">This is easy to see as a disk can be added only when at least one of
                        the opponent&rsquo;s disks swaps its color.</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c51" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">2</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c72" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">The number of disks on the board is the same as the number of moves
                        done on the board so far.</span></p>
                <p class="c13 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c53" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">In each move, exactly one disk is added to the board</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
    </table>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>As a result, let&rsquo;s say that </span><span class="c10">M</span><span>&nbsp;moves have
            been done. This means that </span><span class="c10">M</span><span>&nbsp;disks have been added to the board.
            Let the current connected component of disks be &ldquo;</span><span class="c10">C</span><span>&rdquo;. Let
            &ldquo;</span><span class="c10">R</span><span class="c12">&rdquo; be the smallest rectangle which covers the
            entire connected component. Then, we claim:</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_j8y3zsk6nh9z-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10">Width W of rectangle + Width H of rectangle &lt;= M</span><span
                class="c12">&nbsp;(since in each move, we can either increase the height of rectangle enclosing
                connected component by 1 or we increase width of connected component by 1 or both height and width
                remain the same)</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">In the above example, </span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span
            style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: -0.00px -0.00px; border: 2.67px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 468.74px; height: 456.51px;"><img
                alt="" src="images/image25.png"
                style="width: 468.74px; height: 456.51px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                title=""></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>In the above figure, we see the connected component &ldquo;C&rdquo; is enclosed within the
        </span><span class="c10 c97">RED</span><span>&nbsp;polygon and the smallest rectangle which covers the connected
            component &ldquo;C&rdquo; is enclosed in </span><span class="c10 c124">GREEN</span><span class="c12">.
        </span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">The top-left corner of the rectangle is at cell (4,2).</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">The Bottom right corner of the rectangle is at cell (9,11).</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">In order to represent this configuration, </span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>we would be storing H x W cells (more details on the way these cells are stored mentioned
            later in the doc). Since </span><span class="c10">W+H&lt;=M</span><span>, by </span><span class="c38">AM-GM
            inequality</span><span>, we can say that </span><span class="c10">H x W &lt;= M</span><span
            class="c10 c39">2</span><span class="c21 c10">/4</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c3 c10 c99 c126">Proposal</span><span class="c116 c10 c87 c99 c119">:</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c20">Instead of trying to capture the entire board, we can try to capture only the
            smallest enclosing rectangle. </span><span>For storing a particular state of the game, we can </span><span
            class="c10 c38">store the coordinates of the top-left and bottom-right corner of the
            rectangle</span><span>&nbsp;along with the state of the rectangle (which is empirically MUCH SMALLER as
            compared to the entire board in the INITIAL AND MIDDLE PART OF THE GAME)</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c3 c80 c10 c87 c116">Why would this save a lot of space ?</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>For perspective, for a </span><span class="c10">1000 x 1000 board</span><span
            class="c12">&nbsp;with 1,000,000 cells, </span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p><a id="t.9a63ffae948640020a01b033557c590ddccf58d4"></a><a
        id="t.1"></a>
    <table class="c44">
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c50" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c21 c10">Moves Made</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c82" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c21 c10">Maximum number of cells enclosed by the smallest rectangle
                        enclosing the connected component</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c82" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c21 c10">Fraction of total cells in the board</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c50" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">1</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c82" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">1</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c82" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">1/1e6 = 0.000001</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c50" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">5</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c82" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">7</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c82" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">7/1e6 = 0.000007</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c50" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">15</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c82" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">57 (which is very less as compared to 1e6 ie total number of cells
                        in the board)</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c82" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">57/1e6 = 0.000057</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c50" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">100</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c82" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">2500</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c82" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">2500/1e6 = 0.0025</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
    </table>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c21 c10">Some more examples of the smallest enclosing rectangle:</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span
            style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 4.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 319.74px; height: 319.74px;"><img
                alt="" src="images/image31.png"
                style="width: 319.74px; height: 319.74px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                title=""></span><span
            style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 4.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 361.74px; height: 316.52px;"><img
                alt="" src="images/image7.png"
                style="width: 361.74px; height: 316.52px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                title=""></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10 c87 c96">Feature 2: Encoding rows</span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span>Now, let us store the board row-wise ie calculate an encoding for each row.</span></p>
    <h3 class="c24 c19 c18" id="h.cbn832dcfpnt"><span class="c10 c32 c87 c92">Suggested encoding 1 for rows: </span>
    </h3>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">Let us say that we want to encode row 4 of the board.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">Let B = black, W = white and E = empty</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10">Way V1:</span><span>&nbsp;The current configuration of row 4 in the 12 x 12
            example is : EBBBWWWWWWBE which needs </span><span class="c91">12 characters</span><span
            class="c12">&nbsp;to store</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span
            style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 909.50px; height: 72.61px;"><img
                alt="" src="images/image17.png"
                style="width: 909.50px; height: 72.61px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                title=""></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10">Better way V2:</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;We observe that a lot of
            neighboring characters have the same value and hence, we can prevent some repetition by storing repeated
            values as a pair with entries </span></p>
    <p class="c19 c18 c110"><span class="c21 c10">&lt;number of times a value has been repeated, the repeated
            value&gt;</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>For eg: compressed way of saving row 4 can be </span><span class="c10 c33">1E</span><span
            class="c10 c85">3B</span><span class="c10 c101">6W</span><span class="c10 c66">1B</span><span
            class="c10 c33">1E</span><span>&nbsp;which has </span><span class="c91">10 characters</span><span
            class="c12">&nbsp;only (we store 2 less characters).</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span
            style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 1002.00px; height: 176.00px;"><img
                alt="" src="images/image10.png"
                style="width: 1002.00px; height: 176.00px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                title=""></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12 c63">The amount of characters we will be saving would depend on the number of
            repetitions but given the nature of REVERSI, one expects a lot of neighboring squares to have the same
            values.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10">Improved way V3:</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>A small improvement would be to replace tuples of the form &lt;1, VALUE V&gt; from 1V to
            &ldquo;V&rdquo; only. This does not introduce any ambiguity in our notation. Eg: row 4 will be encoded as:
        </span><span class="c10 c33">E</span><span class="c10 c85">3B</span><span class="c10 c101">6W</span><span
            class="c10 c66">B</span><span class="c10 c33">E </span><span>which has </span><span class="c91">7
            characters</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;only.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">Whenever 2 alphabets are encountered consecutively, we can interpret the
            frequency of the second character to be &ldquo;1&rdquo;. </span></p><a
        id="t.82d8e2e0658fc2562b2bf2810ea1aafe54d3f7a1"></a><a id="t.2"></a>
    <table class="c44">
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c78" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">It is easy to see that way V3 will always occupy less than or equal
                        space when compared to way V1.</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
    </table>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span
            style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 960.50px; height: 168.71px;"><img
                alt="" src="images/image24.png"
                style="width: 960.50px; height: 168.71px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                title=""></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c49 c10 c57">Sample example of page:</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c76 c3 c32 c118">State of the board</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span
            style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: -0.00px -0.00px; border: 2.67px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 373.74px; height: 364.48px;"><img
                alt="" src="images/image25.png"
                style="width: 373.74px; height: 364.48px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                title=""></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c3">Encoding of the different rows:</span></p><a
        id="t.4589d37666578b7d4e287880022ce21ea1894c62"></a><a id="t.3"></a>
    <table class="c44">
        <tr class="c2">

            </td>

            </td>

            </td>
        </tr>

                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">12E</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>

            </td>

            </td>

                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">2E5BE2B2E</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c28" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c30 c18"><span class="c12">Row 8</span></p>
            </td>
