                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">2EBW3B3W2E</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c28" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c30 c18"><span class="c12">Row 9</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c59" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">3E2BEB3W2E</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c28" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c30 c18"><span class="c12">Row 10</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c59" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">12E</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c28" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c30 c18"><span class="c12">Row 11</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c59" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">12E</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c28" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c30 c18"><span class="c12">Row 12</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c59" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">12E</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
    </table>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>Now, </span><span class="c10">let STRING S (with @ as row based delimiter)</span><span
            class="c12">&nbsp;be:</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12 c38">&lt;ENCODING OF row 1 &gt;@&lt;ENCODING OF row 2&gt;...@&lt;ENCODING OF row
            12&gt;</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>This string can be stored directly in pages (can be stored across contiguous pages).</span>
    </p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>We </span><span class="c10 c25">do NOT actually need to store the delimiter</span><span
            class="c12">. The end of the ROW CAN EASILY BE INFERRED WITHOUT DELIMITER as we CAN KEEP TRACK OF THE number
            of cells read so far. The moment we have N cells in a row (N=12 cells for the above example), we can
            interpret a row change.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p><a id="t.5fce6d6bb72597a4965de0dbc7ba0b40dca32054"></a><a
        id="t.4"></a>
    <table class="c44">
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c31" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c21 c10">Without truncation</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c98" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c21 c10">With truncation</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c31" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c5 c18"><span
                        style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: -0.00px -0.00px; border: 2.67px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 308.14px; height: 299.71px;"><img
                            alt="" src="images/image25.png"
                            style="width: 308.14px; height: 299.71px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                            title=""></span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c98" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span
                        style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 302.50px; height: 189.86px;"><img
                            alt="" src="images/image18.png"
                            style="width: 302.50px; height: 189.86px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                            title=""></span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
    </table>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c3 c80 c103 c10 c87">Final string to be stored across pages for the above example
            (WITHOUT TRUNCATION):</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10 c20">12E</span><span class="c20">12E</span><span class="c10 c20">12E</span><span
            class="c20">E3B6WBE</span><span class="c10 c20">2E3WE3BWBE</span><span class="c20">2E8B2E</span><span
            class="c10 c20">2E5BE2B2E</span><span class="c20">2EBW3B3W2E</span><span
            class="c10 c20">3E2BEB3W2E</span><span class="c20">12E</span><span class="c10 c20">12E</span><span
            class="c12 c20">12E</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span
            style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 1002.00px; height: 293.33px;"><img
                alt="" src="images/image1.png"
                style="width: 1002.00px; height: 293.33px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                title=""></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">For ease of reading above, every alternate row&rsquo;s encoding has been bolded.
            Also, we can see that the sum of value frequencies within each row&rsquo;s encoding adds up to 12 which
            helps us detect when a new row starts.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c3 c10">Final string to be stored across pages for the above example </span><span
            class="c3 c10 c42">(after TRUNCATION of the 12 x 12 board into a 6 x 10 rectangle)</span><span
            class="c3 c80 c10 c87 c103">:</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c20">3B6WB</span><span class="c10 c20">E3WE3BWB</span><span
            class="c20">E8BE</span><span class="c10 c20">E5BE2BE</span><span class="c20">EBW3B3WE</span><span
            class="c10 c20">2E2BEB3WE</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10">NOTE: </span><span>T</span><span class="c12">hat this design can be inconvenient
            to visualize/make updates on. That is why we use it only for storage.</span></p>
    <hr>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <h2 class="c19 c18 c117" id="h.363atv494048"><span class="c62 c10">Page Design 2 (Update based Page)</span></h2>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c10">It is not easy to make updates based on moves in the design used in page design
            1</span><span class="c12">. Hence, we switch to a different page design on which updates will be much
            easier. </span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_9ew8pa1jkr1q-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">When a game is being played, its current state &ldquo;S&rdquo;
                will be stored on disk in form of page design 2. </span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">When a move is made, the changes are made in the cells in-place
                i.e. within the same pages.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">When all queries regarding the game has been fulfilled, the
                space allocated to it to store it&rsquo;s boards for updates is EMPTIED. </span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>Let&rsquo;s say a game &ldquo;G&rdquo; has 100 moves and snapshots are already available for
            states after every 10 moves i.e. for (S</span><span class="c15">10</span><span>,S</span><span
            class="c15">20</span><span>&nbsp;,S</span><span class="c15">30</span><span>&nbsp;,S</span><span
            class="c15">40</span><span>&nbsp;,S</span><span class="c15">50</span><span>&nbsp;,S</span><span
            class="c15">60</span><span>&nbsp;, S</span><span class="c15">70</span><span>, S</span><span
            class="c15">80</span><span>, S</span><span class="c15">90</span><span>, S</span><span
            class="c15">100</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;).</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">Let&rsquo;s say a user wants to visualize the game position after move 67 and
            then wants to move step by step till move 68. The following will happen:</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_mh8bkwyuibr4-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">60 is the nearest integer to the left of 67 for which snapshot
                was stored.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span>A copy of the state of the game after move 60 (S</span><span
                class="c15">60</span><span>) is loaded and </span><span class="c25">converted to page design
                2</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;(which is proposed below) and stored into disk (as page with page design
                2).</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Moves 61-67 are executed with changes being made in the copy of
                S60 stored via page design 2. </span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">State of board after game 67 is displayed.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">State of the board is updated (in the copy stored as per page
                design 2) as per move 68.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">State of board after game 68 is displayed.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Now, since the user has left, all the pages (of page design 2)
                corresponding to game &ldquo;G&rdquo; are removed i.e. their storage is freed.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>An important point to note here is, that the storage of the state we will be updating will
            be negligible as compared to the storage of the whole system (millions of game, with each game storing state
            at different checkpoints). </span><span class="c10">This will be only one (temporary) state that will be
            updated again and again.</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">For the 12 x 12 example discussed earlier in the document, </span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">if a row looks like:</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span
            style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 909.50px; height: 72.61px;"><img
                alt="" src="images/image17.png"
                style="width: 909.50px; height: 72.61px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                title=""></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>We&rsquo;ll simply store EBBBWWWWWWBE, </span><span class="c10">without any optimized
            encoding</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;(as opposed to the case of storage-based page design) since optimized
            encoding makes updates complicated.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">Now, since the whole board can&rsquo;t be stored in a single page, we need a way
            to break them. And, there are mainly two ways to do so:</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>Let us consider the following </span><span class="c10">8 x 8</span><span>&nbsp;example (and
            a page size of </span><span class="c10">9 bytes</span><span class="c12">) to demonstrate the design:</span>
    </p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span
            style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: -0.00px -0.00px; border: 2.67px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 494.50px; height: 494.50px;"><img
                alt="" src="images/image3.png"
                style="width: 494.50px; height: 494.50px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                title=""></span></p>
    <h3 class="c24 c19 c18" id="h.7sm4eilb858j"><span class="c3 c10 c87 c100">Proposed update-based page design
            1:</span></h3>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>Fla</span><span>tten the 2D board into a 1D board and store a character
            &ldquo;E&rdquo;,&rdquo;W&rdquo; and &ldquo;B&rdquo; depending on the state of the cell. </span><span>Each
            character occupies one byte. So, if a page can store &ldquo;T&rdquo; bytes, then ceil(N</span><span
            class="c39">2</span><span class="c12">/T) pages will be needed.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c10">String S which can be stored across pages is (alternate rows have been bolded for
            convenience)</span><span class="c12">: </span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c10 c47">EEEWEEEE</span><span class="c47">E</span><span
            class="c57 c65">WWWEEEE</span><span class="c10 c57 c65">EE</span><span
            class="c10 c57 c63">WWEEEE</span><span class="c57 c63">EEW</span><span class="c57 c42">WWWEE</span><span
            class="c10 c57 c42">EEBB</span><span class="c10 c57 c38">WBEE</span><span class="c57 c38">EEBWW</span><span
            class="c48 c57">EEE</span><span class="c10 c57 c48">EBEEEE</span><span class="c46 c10">EE</span><span
            class="c46">EEEEEEE</span><span class="c37 c25 c57 c87">E</span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span>In the above example, different colors represent the contents of different pages assuming a page
            size of 9 bytes.</span></p>
    <h3 class="c24 c19 c18" id="h.n0l0poycqutg"><span class="c3 c80 c10 c87 c109">Proposed update-based page design 2
            (much improved):</span></h3>
    <p class="c5"><span>Store a sub-grid in each page. So if, let&rsquo;s say, the page size allows us to store
        </span><span class="c99">p</span><span>&nbsp;elements, we&rsquo;ll store a grid of </span><span
            class="c99">&radic;p X &radic;p</span><span>&nbsp;in each page. Since we have assumed page size to be 9
            bytes, p =3 for our example.</span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span
            style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: -0.00px -0.00px; border: 1.33px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 616.74px; height: 549.21px;"><img
                alt="" src="images/image15.png"
                style="width: 616.74px; height: 549.21px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                title=""></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>NOTE: Since all elements are fixed length (1 bytes), knowing what page and offset a
            particular cell is present in is straightforward. </span></p>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c115 c80 c87"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c80 c10 c87 c94">We would choose proposed design 2 for our purpose as:</span></p><a
        id="t.8c40b136c8541614bfa77dfef693a7fb6efbb4cf"></a><a id="t.5"></a>
    <table class="c44">
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c56" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c21 c10">Design 1 of flattening the array</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c56" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c21 c10">Design 2 of breaking matrix into submatrices</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c56" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <ul class="c8 lst-kix_oyc3k2xxr2l4-0 start">
                    <li class="c13 c19 c7 li-bullet-0"><span>Row based updates are </span><span class="c10">highly
                            efficient</span><span>&nbsp;as due to the flattening, all elements in the same row are in
                            the same page (or spread across neighboring pages if row size &gt;&gt; page size) resulting
                            in </span><span class="c10">minimal page accesses</span><span class="c12">.</span></li>
                    <li class="c13 c19 c7 li-bullet-0"><span>Column updates &amp; diagonal updates are </span><span
                            class="c10">highly inefficient</span><span class="c12">. 2 neighboring elements in the same
                            column MIGHT BE in different pages, As a result, even updating 2 neighboring elements of the
                            same column can take 2 page accesses.</span></li>
                    <li class="c13 c19 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c106">Locality of reference based advantage present
                            for row-based updates only.</span></li>
                </ul>
            </td>
            <td class="c56" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <ul class="c8 lst-kix_1rx0g9okk7jw-0 start">
                    <li class="c13 c19 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">All updates row--based, column-based and
                            diagonal based are moderately efficient (reasonable number of pages accesses) as most cells
                            are in the same PAGE as their row neighbors, col neighbors and diagonal neighbors.</span>
                    </li>
                    <li class="c13 c19 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c25">Locality of reference based advantage present
                            for all 3 types of updates: row-based col based and diagonal based.</span></li>
                </ul>
            </td>
        </tr>
    </table>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c21 c10"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c3 c10 c45">Another small (but effective) optimization using bits</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>Without much increase in the time or implementation complexity of the state update, we can
            decrease the storage space required. We notice that we are dealing with </span><span class="c10">only 3
            unique characters</span><span class="c12">: B, W and E. We can encode 3 unique characters with just 2
            bits.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>So, instead of using an entire character (1 byte) &nbsp;for each state, we can represent
            them using 2 bits </span><span class="c10">(</span><span class="c10 c38">4 fold reduction in
            space</span><span class="c10">). </span><span class="c12">See the below table for more details:</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p><a id="t.18b187cb835d70114926d853f422ed477307fe0d"></a><a
        id="t.6"></a>
    <table class="c44">
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c61" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c21 c10">STATE</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c61" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span>Earlier representation </span><span class="c21 c10">(8 bits)</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c61" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span>Proposed bit representation </span><span class="c21 c10">(2 bits)</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c68">
            <td class="c61" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">WHITE CELL</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c61" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">ascii of &lsquo;W&rsquo;: 01010111</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c61" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">01</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c61" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">BLACK CELL</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c61" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">ascii of &lsquo;B&rsquo;: 01000010</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c61" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">10</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c61" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">EMPTY CELL</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c61" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">ascii of &lsquo;E&rsquo;: 01000101</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c61" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">00</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
    </table>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">This data can simply be treated as bit stream, which can then be encoded into
            bytes for storage (explained in detail below).</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <h2 class="c117 c19 c18" id="h.7ni2xdu38yqw"><span class="c62 c10">Storing the moves of each game in a new
            relation</span></h2>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>Let each game have a GAME ID which is </span><span class="c10">incremental </span><span>in
            nature. For resolving the state of the board between checkpoints (intermediate states), all moves of the
            game need to be stored. For this, we maintain a separate table with this page design as explained in
            &ldquo;proposed approach&rdquo;:</span><span class="c10">&nbsp;Since the player turns are alternative, we
            need not store the player ID of the player who made the move (</span><span>an even move is always by player
            1 and odd move is always by player 2</span><span class="c10">).</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c21 c10">Proposed Approach</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_xn87byvarnls-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Each move can be uniquely identified by which cell the disk was
                placed: &nbsp;a (row, column) pair.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Instead of adding a separator between row and column (and,
                between moves), we&rsquo;ll keep them fixed size. This will also help to optimize queries like what was
                the 1000th move.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">It&rsquo;s tempting to store the number as a normal integer (or
                a string), it&rsquo;ll take 4 bytes. So, a total of 8 bytes will be used per move.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c21 c10">But, we&rsquo;ll store the sequence of moves as a sequence
                of bits.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span>Since the number (row or column) can go upto 1000, </span><span
                class="c38">10 bits will be enough to store a row or column number</span><span>&nbsp;(since
                2</span><span class="c39">10</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;= 1024 &gt; 1000).</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span>So, in total, storing the location of a cell (and hence, also one move) will
                require only </span><span class="c21 c10">20 bits or 2.5 bytes.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c21 c10">Example:</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">Consider an arbitrary (not necessarily valid) sequence of moves: </span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10">Move 1:</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;Black disk placed at (1,2) </span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10">Move 2:</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;White disk placed at (5,6)</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10">Move 3:</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;Black disk placed at (934,40)</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10">Move 4:</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;White disk placed at (20,676)</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">The 10 bit representation of the numbers are shown in the table.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p><a id="t.d121c5080475572192ab720a6d8a596c86e0405d"></a><a
        id="t.7"></a>
    <table class="c64">
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c36" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c21 c10">Number</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c83" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c21 c10">Binary Representation (10 bits fixed length)</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c36" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">1</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c83" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">0000000001</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c36" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">2</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c83" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">0000000010</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c36" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">5</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c83" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">0000000101</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c36" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">6</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c83" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">0000000110</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c36" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">934</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c83" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">1110100110</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c36" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">40</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c83" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">0000101000</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c36" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">20</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c83" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">0000010100</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c36" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">676</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c83" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c12">1010100100</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
    </table>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c12">So, the bit sequence will be:</span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c10 c65">0000000001</span><span class="c3 c65">0000000010</span><span
            class="c10 c42">0000000101</span><span class="c3 c42">0000000110</span><span
            class="c10 c48">1110100110</span><span class="c3 c48">0000101000</span><span
            class="c10 c113">0000010100</span><span class="c76 c3 c80 c113">1010100100</span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">(different moves are separated by different highlight color, with bold as row
            number and underlined as column number)</span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18"><span
            style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 840.74px; height: 210.64px;"><img
                alt="" src="images/image14.png"
                style="width: 840.74px; height: 210.64px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                title=""></span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18"><span>Now, to store this bit sequence, we can </span><span class="c10">group them into sizes of
            8</span><span class="c12">, and store its character representation. So, the above bit sequence will be
            grouped as:</span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">(00000000) (01000000) (00100000) (00010100) (00000110) (11101001) (10000010)
            (10000000) (01010010) (10100100)</span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c21 c10">When converted to integers, it&rsquo;ll become: 0 64 32 20 6 233 130 128 82
            164</span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">Now, we can use these integers as ASCII value for the characters we&rsquo;ll
            store (we don&rsquo;t show them here as some of them are not printable).</span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">As we can see, we store 10 characters (= 10 bytes) for storing 4 moves. While
            reading, we can simply decode the characters back to bit string and then find the required row and column
            number.</span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c76 c3 c80">In the page for this relation, one can continually store the elements
            ordered by GAME ID as:</span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18"><span>&lt;Game Id 1&gt;</span><span class="c10 c38">:</span><span>&lt;Unfixed length bit string
            of moves&gt;</span><span class="c10 c38">&amp;</span><span class="c12">&lt;Game Id 2&gt;:&lt;Unfixed length
            bit string of moves&gt; &hellip;&hellip;&hellip;. and so on</span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">Since an element of such a relation CANNOT be modified after insertion,
            maintaining an ordered unfixed relation is easy. </span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18"><span class="c12">Additional data may be stored per page to store information such as the list of
            game IDs whose moves are present within the page and so on.</span></p>
    <hr>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <h2 class="c6" id="h.7ggxhgmo8j95"><span class="c62 c10">To store one completed game, how much storage is needed.
        </span></h2>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c12">I have given stepwise memory consumed by the different steps of the pipeline in
            respective sections. Recapping:</span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c10">Let size of board</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;: N x N</span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c10">Total number of moves</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;= TotMoves</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c10">Term 1:</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;Memory consumed to store the moves</span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c10">Ans:</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;a 4 byte fixed length integer to store the game
            ID + 2 one byte delimiters + TotMoves x 2.5 bytes </span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c12">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;= 4 + 2 + TotMoves x 2.5
            &nbsp;= 6 + (TotMoves x 2.5)</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c10">Term 2:</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;Storing snapshots of the game</span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span>Basically, since we are storing the smallest sized rectangle for the checkpoints. We are storing
            k = &radic;TotMoves ~ N checkpoints and each checkpoint would occupy atmax N</span><span
            class="c39">2</span><span class="c15">&nbsp;</span><span class="c12">bytes (one for each cell of the board)
            at worst (I have provided a better bound using AM-GM equality in the detailed section).</span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c10">The worst memory needed here: N</span><span class="c10 c39">3</span><span
            class="c21 c10">&nbsp;approx</span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c12">Usually, much less memory would be needed here due to the compression of neighboring
            cells in the same row.</span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c12">We would also need (4 x &radic;TotMoves) bytes to store the coordinates of the
            corners of the rectangles as well.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c10">Term 3:</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;Storage needed to navigate the game in real
            time (temporary storage ie can be relinquished after user has finished analyzed the game)</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">There are N x N cells. Assuming a character based encoding of empty, white and
            black, each cell will occupy one byte. </span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">Let a page be capable of storing &ldquo;p&rdquo; bytes. Then, it can store
            &radic;p elements across either dimension.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">Therefore, memory needed would be: </span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10">[ceil(N/&radic;p)]</span><span class="c10 c39">2 </span><span class="c10">x
            p</span><span class="c21 c10">&nbsp;</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c21 c10"></span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c10">Total memory = </span><span class="c12">sum of all the above terms</span></p>
    <h2 class="c6" id="h.9j2wd6mbjp2v"><span>Summarizing, </span></h2>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c21 c10">Recapping the various benefits of our design,</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_nt32fxhuubg5-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Due to truncation + compression in the storage based page design
                (#1), we are storing as minimal storage as needed per snapshot.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">The feature of taking snapshots is helping us answer queries of
                type Q3 very efficiently .</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">The usage of page design (#2) for updates makes updates
                extremely quick. Storing the square submatrices in each page instead of flattening the board grid helps
                us take advantage of locality of reference during disk-page accesses for all 3 types of updates:
                row-based, column-based and diagonal based updates. This is especially helpful for Reversi where all
                updates are on contiguous neighboring cells possible across all 6 directions.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Using Huffman encoding based compression for WHITE, BLACK and
                EMPTY helps us reduce our storage for the state of each board cell by 4 times (from 1 byte to 2
                bits).</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c19 c18 c74 title" id="h.je17rbg40voj"><span class="c10 c71">Page &amp; Algorithm Design for Query
            Execution for assisting Reversi/Othello players</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_1yrga9xxgdih-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Anmol Agarwal (2019101068), Sanchit Arora (2019101047)</span>
        </li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c17 c105"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c49 c10 c32">Some terminology/notation:</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_pujfjsp62b1z-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10">N</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;= side of the board =&gt; N x N
                = number of cells on the board | N&lt;=1e3</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c65">For ease of reference, without loss of generality, we consider
                the initial configuration of the board played i.e. having 4 disks as the first four moves</span><span
                class="c12">. Hence, MAX MOVES in our case: N x N (since we are considering the initial configuration of
                the game to consume 4 moves)</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10">G</span><span class="c12">: game ID</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10">TotMoves:</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;total number of moves
                played in the game.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10 c29">M</span><span class="c10 c29 c15">i</span><span
                class="c12">: ith move of the game where 1&lt;=i&lt;=TotMoves. (NOTE: M1, M2, M3 and M4 are fixed since
                they correspond to the initial configuration of the game)</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10">S</span><span class="c10 c15">i</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;=
                state of the board after Move &ldquo;i&rdquo;</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10 c29">TotGames</span><span class="c12">: Total number of games in
                the database so far</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">K = Number of nearest neighbours to be considered (Let
                k&lt;=50)</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c32">Intermediate_K: number of nearest neighbours retained in the
                pruning step: </span><span>(let Intermediate_K be of the order &lt;= 500)</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12 c20"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c49 c10 c4"></span></p>
    <p class="c19 c18 c114 title" id="h.ow2qfqo6ms98"><span class="c49 c10 c58">Approach to finding K nearest Neighbours
            and revised page design:</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c94 c10 c87 c118 c125">Part 0: Defining a subproblem whose solution helps us solve
            the later part of the assignment</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c0">First, we will describe a new unrelated subproblem and then, we will use
            subproblem in our method to find the K nearest neighbours.</span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c10 c4">Subproblem: </span><span class="c4">Let V = {V</span><span
            class="c4 c15">1</span><span class="c4">, &hellip;, V</span><span class="c4 c15">t </span><span class="c4">}
            be a set of &ldquo;t&rdquo; vectors, each having &ldquo;d&rdquo; dimensions. We need to find the
        </span><span class="c4 c65">&ldquo;S&#39;&#39; approximate nearest neighbours</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;to a
            new query vector V</span><span class="c4 c15">query</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;.</span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c49 c10 c4">Approach: </span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c4">Inspired by </span><span class="c3 c4 c85"><a class="c75"
                href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://ai.facebook.com/tools/faiss/&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1671217651812534&amp;usg=AOvVaw3zWItvRmlKZTUb1H4SXdPZ">FAISS</a></span><span
            class="c4">&nbsp;and </span><span class="c3 c4 c85"><a class="c75"
                href="https://www.google.com/url?q=http://philogb.github.io/blog/2010/02/12/voronoi-tessellation/?utm_source%3Dfeedburner&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1671217651812960&amp;usg=AOvVaw3n7V8hTTSTsn1VpcotxVCO">Voronoi
                Tessellation</a></span><span class="c0">, we solve this problem in the following way:</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_nrh864je400p-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">For the sake of our example, we consider &ldquo;t&rdquo; to be
                &ldquo;100&rdquo;.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c3 c4">STEP 1 &nbsp;(</span><span class="c3 c10 c4">One time
                preprocessing step</span><span class="c3 c4">) :</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;Firstly, we cluster these
                &ldquo;t&rdquo; vectors into some predetermined &ldquo;J&rdquo; number of clusters and denote
                C</span><span class="c4 c15">j</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;as the centroid of the vectors belonging in
                the jth cluster.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5"><span
            style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: -0.00px -0.00px; border: 1.33px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 864.00px; height: 517.33px;"><img
                alt="" src="images/image32.png"
                style="width: 864.00px; height: 517.33px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                title=""></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_4w79krz3a57c-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">In the above diagram, &ldquo;J&rdquo; i.e. number of clusters =
                15.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_4w79krz3a57c-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Vectors V</span><span class="c4 c15">1 </span><span class="c4">,
                V</span><span class="c4 c15">2</span><span class="c4">, </span><span class="c4 c15">&nbsp;</span><span
                class="c4">V</span><span class="c4 c15">44 </span><span class="c4">V</span><span class="c4 c15">35
            </span><span class="c4">V</span><span class="c4 c15">50 </span><span class="c4">belong to cluster ID: 7 ;
                &nbsp;C</span><span class="c4 c15">7</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;is the centroid of the included
                vectors.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Vectors V</span><span class="c4 c15">3 </span><span class="c4">,
                V</span><span class="c4 c15">7</span><span class="c4">, </span><span class="c4 c15">&nbsp;</span><span
                class="c4">V</span><span class="c4 c15">95 </span><span class="c4">V</span><span class="c4 c15">71
                &nbsp;</span><span class="c4">belong to cluster ID: 8 ; C</span><span class="c4 c15">8</span><span
                class="c0">&nbsp;is the centroid of the included vectors.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_4w79krz3a57c-0">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c3 c4">STEP 2:</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;Now, instead of naively
                searching for the nearest neighbour for V</span><span class="c4 c15">query </span><span class="c0">by
                comparing it with all &ldquo;t&rdquo; vectors, we compare it with only the &ldquo;J&rdquo; centroids
                (J&lt;&lt;t) and determine the cluster whose centroid is closest to it. Let&rsquo;s the closest cluster
                have ID: &ldquo;ClosestCluster&rdquo;</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c3 c4">STEP 3:</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;Then, we now, calculate
                the &ldquo;S&rdquo; nearest neighbours of &nbsp;V</span><span class="c4 c15">query </span><span
                class="c0">by comparing it with all members of cluster having ID:
                &nbsp;&ldquo;ClosestCluster&rdquo;</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c0">In order to retrieve vector members of the closest cluster (ID:
            &ldquo;ClosestCluster&rdquo; ) ie STEP 3, we maintain a table with rows values: &lt;Vector ID, Cluster ID in
            which vector is present&gt;.</span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c4">For efficient retrieval, we maintain a </span><span class="c10 c4 c38">secondary
            index</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;on the attribute (Clustering ID ie &nbsp;</span><span
            class="c10 c48 c4">nonkey, nonordering field</span><span class="c48 c4">&nbsp;</span><span class="c4">)
            where we store the following attribute in the secondary index: &lt;Clustering ID, </span><span
            class="c10 c4">block pointer</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;to block containing vector IDs belonging to
            &nbsp;the cluster&gt;</span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c0"><br>For the above illustration, our secondary index has the following structure:
        </span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span
            style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: -0.00px 0.00px; border: 2.67px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 609.08px; height: 414.50px;"><img
                alt="" src="images/image21.png"
                style="width: 609.08px; height: 414.50px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                title=""></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c4">NOTE: if we wish to add newly played games to this index, we can </span><span
            class="c10 c4">lazily</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;update/recreate the clusters after every &ldquo;H&rdquo;
            new games.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c49 c10 c4">Query answering Time complexity : </span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c4">O(</span><span class="c1">dimensions in each vector</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;X
        </span><span class="c1">number of clusters</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;) + &nbsp;O(</span><span
            class="c1">dimensions in each vector</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;X </span><span class="c1">number of
            vectors in selected cluster</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;) + O(Number of block accesses in the secondary
            index)</span></p>
    <hr>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <hr>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <hr>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <h3 class="c24 c19 c18" id="h.68k08xj1t5l0"><span class="c55 c10">Part 1: What are the desirable properties our
            similarity metric should cover ?</span></h3>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c4">The metric should show high similarity for S</span><span class="c4 c15">G,
            i</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;with S</span><span class="c4 c15">G, i</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;itself
            but also with the below versions of S</span><span class="c4 c15">G, i</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;after
        </span><span class="c4 c65">rotation, flipping, colour inversion etc</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;as can be seen
            below.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p><a id="t.370fe1201ee44feeef24cc1515425078c450ff61"></a><a
        id="t.8"></a>
