    <hr>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <h2 class="c6" id="h.8byrsmynz3m3"><span class="c4 c95">Part 2: Candidates for base exact similarity metric between
            2 given states ie board configuration: P and Q ie BaseExactSim(</span><span class="c4 c90">P, Q</span><span
            class="c93 c10 c87 c4">)</span></h2>
    <h3 class="c24 c19 c18" id="h.s8jg3lryr8u9"><span class="c55 c10 c38">Choice 1 for &ldquo;Base Exact Similarity
            Metric&rdquo;: Number of unmatching cells needed</span></h3>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c0 c20"></span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_6k1xvs9c2d5p-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Given states P and Q (each with N x N elements), when using this
                metric, we define </span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_6k1xvs9c2d5p-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Let state of cell (i,j, P) = state of cell(i,j) in game state
                &ldquo;P&rdquo; =:</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_6k1xvs9c2d5p-2 start">
        <li class="c5 c54 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">0 if the cell is white</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c54 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">1 if cell is black</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c54 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">2 if cell is empty</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_6k1xvs9c2d5p-1">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10 c4">BaseExactSim(P, Q) :</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;number of
                cells in (i,j) where </span><span class="c3 c1 c76">state(i,j,P)!=state(i,j,Q)</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c76 c3 c1"></span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c10 c91 c4">Time complexity</span><span class="c10 c4">&nbsp;(</span><span
            class="c4">Assuming that states P and Q are already in main meory</span><span class="c10 c4 c49">):</span>
    </p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_z3vxrdsiqm0u-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Checking each cell will require </span><span
                class="c52 c1">O(1)</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">There are total </span><span class="c1">N</span><span
                class="c1 c39">2</span><span class="c1">&nbsp;</span><span class="c0">cells</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Therefore, time-complexity = </span><span
                class="c1">O(N</span><span class="c1 c39">2</span><span class="c1">)</span></li>
    </ul>
    <h3 class="c24 c19 c18" id="h.l4t2qpi2lut"><span class="c43 c10 c38">Choice 2 for &ldquo;Base Exact Similarity
            Metric&rdquo;: Jaccard based similarity</span></h3>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10 c4">Metric proposal</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_5acizy6shw0l-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Jaccard Row Similarity:</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_5acizy6shw0l-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Let R</span><span class="c4 c15">P</span><span
                class="c0">&nbsp;= set of unique rows in board configuration &ldquo;P&rdquo;</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Let R</span><span class="c4 c15">Q</span><span
                class="c0">&nbsp;= set of unique rows in board configuration &ldquo;Q&rdquo;</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10 c4">Jaccard_Rows(P, Q)</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;=
            </span><span
                style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 104.00px; height: 67.00px;"><img
                    alt="" src="images/image28.png"
                    style="width: 104.00px; height: 67.00px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                    title=""></span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_5acizy6shw0l-0">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Similarly, Jaccard Column Similarity:</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_5acizy6shw0l-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Let C</span><span class="c4 c15">P</span><span
                class="c0">&nbsp;= set of unique rows in board configuration &ldquo;P&rdquo;</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Let C</span><span class="c4 c15">Q</span><span
                class="c0">&nbsp;= set of unique rows in board configuration &ldquo;Q&rdquo;</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10 c4">Jaccard_Cols(P, Q)</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;=
            </span><span
                style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 148.00px; height: 91.00px;"><img
                    alt="" src="images/image6.png"
                    style="width: 148.00px; height: 91.00px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                    title=""></span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_5acizy6shw0l-0">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Then, </span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_5acizy6shw0l-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10 c4">BaseExactSim(P, Q) :</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;Total
                Jaccard Similarity = </span><span class="c49 c10 c4">Jaccard_Rows(P, Q) + Jaccard_Cols(P, Q)</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c49 c10 c4"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c3 c10 c4 c60">How can (R</span><span class="c3 c10 c4 c60 c15">P</span><span
            class="c3 c10 c4 c60">&nbsp;U R</span><span class="c3 c10 c4 c15 c60">Q</span><span
            class="c4 c60">)</span><span class="c3 c10 c4 c60">&nbsp; and (R</span><span
            class="c3 c10 c4 c60 c15">P</span><span class="c3 c10 c4 c60">&nbsp;&cap;R</span><span
            class="c3 c10 c4 c60 c15">Q </span><span class="c4 c60">) </span><span
            class="c3 c10 c87 c4 c60 c118 c122">be calculated ?</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_m7c6tqlky7wl-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Each row is a sequence : E,W,B depending on whether the cells in
                the row are white, black or empty.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">We can convert this string of E,W and B into a binary string
                using </span><span class="c25 c4">Huffman Compression</span><span class="c0">. </span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_m7c6tqlky7wl-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 c17 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12"></span></li>
    </ul><a id="t.4f594cb41492b6096c049233c4f64b07010af555"></a><a id="t.9"></a>
    <table class="c44">
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c56" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c22"><span class="c21 c10">STATE</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c56" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c22"><span>Proposed bit representation </span><span class="c21 c10">(2 bits)</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c68">
            <td class="c56" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c22"><span class="c12">WHITE CELL (W)</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c56" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c22"><span class="c12">01</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c56" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c22"><span class="c12">BLACK CELL (B)</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c56" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c22"><span class="c12">10</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c56" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c22"><span class="c12">EMPTY CELL (E)</span></p>
            </td>
            <td class="c56" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13 c22"><span class="c12">00</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
    </table>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10 c4">Our solution:</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;Now that we can represent rows as
            binary strings, we can calculate intersections and unions using </span><span class="c20 c4">Dynamic Hashing
            OR Extendible Hashing on the binary strings</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;(Essentially, we are interested in
            using a Trie type data structure. But since we cannot fit a trie in memory, we use the database equivalent
            of tries ie Extendible Hashing based data structure. )</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10 c4">Calculating number of elements in </span><span
            class="c3 c4 c10">&nbsp;(R</span><span class="c3 c10 c4 c15">P</span><span class="c3 c10 c4">&nbsp;U
            R</span><span class="c3 c10 c4 c15">Q</span><span class="c4">)</span><span class="c49 c10 c4">:</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_723z8x6uz4lz-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">First, the hash data structure is empty.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Iterate through all rows of R</span><span
                class="c4 c15">P</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;and insert into the data structure if the row already does
                not exist. If the row already does not exist, insert UnionCnt by 1.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Iterate through all rows of R</span><span
                class="c4 c15">Q</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;and insert into the data structure if rows already does
                not exist. If the row already does not exist, insert UnionCnt by 1.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10 c4">Calculating number of elements in </span><span
            class="c3 c10 c4">&nbsp;(R</span><span class="c3 c10 c4 c15">P</span><span class="c3 c10 c4">&nbsp; &cap;
            R</span><span class="c3 c10 c4 c15">Q</span><span class="c4">)</span><span class="c49 c10 c4">:</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_723z8x6uz4lz-0">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">First, create 2 extendible hash data structures (H1 and H2) is
                empty.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Iterate through all rows of R</span><span
                class="c4 c15">P</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;and insert into the data structure H1 if the row already
                does not exist.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Iterate through all rows of R</span><span
                class="c4 c15">Q</span><span class="c0">.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_723z8x6uz4lz-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">If the row existed in H1 but not in H2. </span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_723z8x6uz4lz-2 start">
        <li class="c5 c54 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Then, increment IntersectCnt by 1.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c54 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Insert row in H2.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c4">The Jaccard Value can be calculated using: </span><span
            class="c10 c4">UnionCnt</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;and </span><span
            class="c49 c10 c4">IntersectCnt.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c49 c10 c4"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c49 c10 c4"></span></p><a id="t.acb43d82952f7acb25d08ec7903b22c4f2f636a1"></a><a
        id="t.10"></a>
    <table class="c44">
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c78" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c49 c10 c4">Example:</span></p>
                <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p><a
                    id="t.43f5925f25d8ee784030663eb05a1c7a037539be"></a><a id="t.11"></a>
                <table class="c44">
                    <tr class="c2">
                        <td class="c111" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                            <p class="c30 c18"><span class="c0">Board 1 (P)</span></p>
                        </td>
                        <td class="c111" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                            <p class="c30 c18"><span class="c0">Board 2 (Q)</span></p>
                        </td>
                    </tr>
                    <tr class="c2">
                        <td class="c111" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                            <p class="c13 c18"><span
                                    style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 418.00px; height: 418.67px;"><img
                                        alt="" src="images/image27.png"
                                        style="width: 418.00px; height: 418.67px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                                        title=""></span></p>
                        </td>
                        <td class="c111" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                            <p class="c13 c18"><span
                                    style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 428.22px; height: 424.17px;"><img
                                        alt="" src="images/image12.png"
                                        style="width: 428.22px; height: 424.17px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                                        title=""></span></p>
                        </td>
                    </tr>
                </table>
                <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
                <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c0">In the above example, as shown with the matching colours, these
                        match:</span></p>
                <ul class="c8 lst-kix_6mbac4y36vdw-0 start">
                    <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Row 6 in Board 1 with Row 4 in Board 2</span></li>
                    <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Column 2 in Board 1 with Column 4 in Board 2</span>
                    </li>
                    <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Column 11 in Board 1 with Column 5 in Board 2</span>
                    </li>
                    <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">All empty rows/columns</span></li>
                </ul>
                <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
                <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c0">Jaccard_Rows = 2/12 = 1/6</span></p>
                <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c0">Jaccard_Cols = 3/19</span></p>
                <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c4">BaseExactSim = 1/6 + 3/19 = 0.32456</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
    </table>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c49 c10 c4"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c49 c10 c91 c4">Time complexity:</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_jrksq4kfu63r-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Total number of rows in each state = </span><span
                class="c1">N</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Hashing each row will require iterating through each row element
                (i.e. number of columns), therefore </span><span class="c52 c1">O(N)</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Therefore, time-complexity of creating the extendible hashing
                data structure = </span><span class="c1">O(N</span><span class="c1 c39">2</span><span
                class="c52 c1">)</span></li>
    </ul>
    <hr>
    <h2 class="c6 c27" id="h.2tozqrozap1n"><span class="c10 c87 c4 c93"></span></h2>
    <h2 class="c6" id="h.cogq1nqhwm66"><span class="c93 c10 c87 c4">Part 3: Defining alternate states of a state of the
            game</span></h2>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_63dqtq9abjai-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Let </span><span class="c4 c38">Variations(S</span><span
                class="c4 c38 c15">G,i</span><span class="c4 c38">)</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;= set of states =
                {S</span><span class="c4 c39">90</span><span class="c4 c15">G, i</span><span
                class="c4">&nbsp;,S</span><span class="c4 c39">180</span><span class="c4 c15">G, i</span><span
                class="c4">&nbsp;, S</span><span class="c4 c39">270</span><span class="c4 c15">G, i</span><span
                class="c4">&nbsp;, S</span><span class="c4 c39">V</span><span class="c4 c15">G, i</span><span
                class="c4">&nbsp;,S</span><span class="c4 c39">H</span><span class="c4 c15">G, i</span><span
                class="c4">&nbsp;, S</span><span class="c4 c39">D1</span><span class="c4 c15">G, i</span><span
                class="c4">&nbsp;, S</span><span class="c4 c39">D2</span><span class="c4 c15">G, i</span><span
                class="c0">}</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Then, let us define </span><span
                class="c10 c4">&nbsp;</span><span class="c10 c4 c38">Alts(S</span><span
                class="c10 c4 c38 c15">G,i</span><span class="c10 c4 c38">)</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;=
                Variations(S</span><span class="c4 c15">G,i</span><span class="c4">) U Variations(S</span><span
                class="c10 c4 c39">#</span><span class="c4 c15">G,i</span><span class="c0">)</span></li>
    </ul>
    <hr>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c49 c10 c4"></span></p>
    <h2 class="c6" id="h.mknr68ly2r2g"><span class="c93 c10 c87 c4">Part 4: Pruning the search space for shortlisting
            candidates at move &ldquo;i&rdquo;:</span></h2>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_gycizvnah24u-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Recapping from our previous submission, for a game
                &ldquo;G&rdquo;, with TotMoves total moves, we were storing checkpoints of the game state after every
                &radic;TotMoves. This helped us to retrieve the state of the game at any move &ldquo;i&rdquo; in
                O(&radic;TotMoves) [how ?: explained in previous submission]</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">For a game &ldquo;G&rdquo; with 100 total moves, we store a
                checkpoint every 10 moves.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_gycizvnah24u-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span
                style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 828.00px; height: 301.00px;"><img
                    alt="" src="images/image9.png"
                    style="width: 828.00px; height: 301.00px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                    title=""></span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c13 c18 c19"><span class="c3 c10 c4 c33">Proposed algorithm for finding the K nearest neighbours of the
            ith state of game G ie </span><span class="c3 c10 c108 c33">S</span><span
            class="c3 c10 c33 c15 c108">G,i</span></p>
    <h3 class="c34 c19 c18" id="h.up9jpcrk408r"><span class="c55 c10">Inputs:</span></h3>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_w808i5q8di03-0 start">
        <li class="c13 c19 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c37 c79">Game ID: G</span></li>
        <li class="c13 c19 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c37 c79">State ID: i</span></li>
        <li class="c13 c19 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c89">State of the game: S</span><span class="c89 c15">G,i</span>
        </li>
    </ul>
    <h3 class="c19 c18 c34" id="h.38ngo5fcw6u2"><span class="c55 c10">Some notation:</span></h3>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_h3tt7acksgzy-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">TotGames: number of games played in the past</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">N : size of game board</span></li>
    </ul>
    <h3 class="c34 c19 c18" id="h.wwq2r66hmnws"><span class="c55 c10">Preprocessing:</span></h3>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_i2xz172pc2wa-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">For </span><span class="c10 c4">EACH</span><span
                class="c0">&nbsp;move IDs &ldquo;M&rdquo; in {0, &radic;TotMoves, &nbsp;2 * &radic;TotMoves, &hellip;,
                &radic;TotMoves x &radic;TotMoves }, </span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_i2xz172pc2wa-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">create a voronoi based index (as in part 0) using flattened
                vectors of {S</span><span class="c4 c15">G1,M , </span><span class="c4">&hellip;, S</span><span
                class="c4 c15">GTotGames,M </span><span class="c4">} </span><span class="c10 c4">and their variations
            </span><span class="c10 c4 c38">Alts(S</span><span class="c10 c4 c38 c15">G,i</span><span
                class="c10 c4 c38">)</span><span class="c4 c38">&nbsp;[as described in Section 3]</span><span
                class="c0">&nbsp;in with total &ldquo;TotGames&rdquo; vectors with &ldquo;N x N&rdquo; dimensions each
                with each vector element being: </span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_i2xz172pc2wa-2 start">
        <li class="c5 c54 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">0 if white</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c54 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">1 if black</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c54 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">2 if empty</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_i2xz172pc2wa-0">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">There will be &radic;TotMoves such voronoi based indexes.</span>
        </li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c17 c121"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span
            style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: -0.00px 0.00px; border: 2.67px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 864.00px; height: 280.00px;"><img
                alt="" src="images/image11.png"
                style="width: 864.00px; height: 280.00px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                title=""></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10 c4">Algorithm</span><span class="c0">:</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_jl3twyajlkch-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Initially, there are TotGames candidates for nearest
                neighbours.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">We reduced number of candidates from &ldquo;TotGames&rdquo; to
                &ldquo;Intermediate_K&rdquo; by:</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_jl3twyajlkch-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Let </span><span class="c0 c25">move &ldquo;M&rdquo; be nearest
                move to &ldquo;i&rdquo; at which checkpoint was taken</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Heuristically, find the &ldquo;Intermediate_K&rdquo; nearest
                neighbours of S</span><span class="c4 c15">G,M </span><span class="c4">(NOTE: this is NOT using
                S</span><span class="c4 c15">G,i</span><span class="c4">) via the Voronoi index constructed at move
                &ldquo;M&rdquo; using </span><span class="c49 c10 c4">Part 0.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10 c4">Stats:</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_jl3twyajlkch-2 start">
        <li class="c5 c54 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Block accesses:</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_jl3twyajlkch-3 start">
        <li class="c5 c77 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">T1: O( (N x N) X </span><span class="c3 c4">number of
                clusters</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;) to find nearest cluster</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c77 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">T2: O(log(Number of blocks in secondary index)) + O(Number of
                blocks containing vectors of selected cluster)</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c77 li-bullet-0"><span class="c49 c10 c4">Ans: T1 + T2</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_jl3twyajlkch-1">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">NOTE: these filtered neighbours, include all variations of a
                board: ie rotations, ,flips etc.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_jl3twyajlkch-0">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Now, for each of these &ldquo;Intermediate_K&rdquo; neighbours,
                find the similarity using one of the COMPUTATIONALLY COSTLY choices of: </span><span
                class="c10 c95 c4">BaseExactSim(</span><span class="c4">P, Q</span><span class="c10 c95 c4">)
            </span><span class="c0">described in Part 2.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_jl3twyajlkch-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c49 c10 c4">Stats:</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_jl3twyajlkch-2 start">
        <li class="c5 c54 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Block accesses:</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_jl3twyajlkch-3 start">
        <li class="c5 c77 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">T1: O(N^2/p) for calculating similarity of S</span><span
                class="c4 c15">G,i </span><span class="c0">with a candidate [refer to previous submission for
                &ldquo;p&rdquo;]</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c77 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10 c20 c4">Total: </span><span class="c0 c20">T1 x (number of
                intermediate neighbours)</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_jl3twyajlkch-1">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Among these &ldquo;Intermediate_K&rdquo; neighbours,
            </span><span class="c10 c4">choose the final K nearest</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;boards using after
                sorting per &ldquo;BaseExactSim(S</span><span class="c4 c15">G,i</span><span class="c0">, Neighbour
                N)&rdquo;.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <hr>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c49 c10 c4"></span></p>
    <p class="c114 c19 c18 title" id="h.2xv983kp82xy"><span class="c10 c35">ANSWERING QUERIES</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c0">For the rest of the assignment, let us consider that the player is making queries
            while the game is currently at move &ldquo;C&rdquo;.</span></p>
    <h1 class="c19 c18 c112" id="h.8y4n20fjeiis"><span class="c10 c43">Part 5: Page Design</span></h1>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p><a id="t.84737da0f8432eebda51aa234f68df33fed82967"></a><a
        id="t.12"></a>
    <table class="c44">
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c78" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c49 c10 c4">Preserving previous Page Design: </span></p>
                <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c0">We&rsquo;ll be keeping our page design as proposed in the previous
                        part as it is, i.e. we will be keeping: &ldquo;storage based page design&rdquo; and
                        &ldquo;update based page design&rdquo; as it is.</span></p>
                <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
                <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c49 c10 c4">Adding new page designs: </span></p>
                <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c4">Other than that, we&rsquo;ll be storing some </span><span
                        class="c25 c4">extra pages</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;for each game to optimise the new
                        queries. The details for the new page design is below:</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
    </table>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c4">For each board, at each checkpoint, for each cell </span><span
            class="c1">(i,j)</span><span class="c0">, we&rsquo;ll be storing the number of flips. As we do with the
            state of games, i.e. use the state stored at checkpoints to generate any intermediate state required,
            we&rsquo;ll do the same for the number of flips as well.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c21 c10">Storing number of flips:</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">We have two options for storing number of flips at each checkpoint:</span></p>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_ncole9hsqbxz-0 start" start="1">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Store the number of flips from the starting of the game till the
                last move of that checkpoint.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c12">Store the number of flips that happened after the last
                checkpoint.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">Considering the size of the board we&rsquo;re considering (i.e. of the order
            1000 X 1000), and the nature of the game, there will be many cells that won&rsquo;t change much after every
            checkpoint.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10">So, at one checkpoint we&rsquo;ll store, let&rsquo;s say, 1000 flips and now
            even if there is no change we&rsquo;ll keep storing 1000 (or 100x if let&rsquo;s say there are &lt;= 9
            flips). This results in storing unnecessarily high numbers, that too, for each cell, whereas in the
            2</span><span class="c10 c39">nd</span><span class="c21 c10">&nbsp;approach, we can store smaller numbers (1
            digit in case of the example).</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">Now let&rsquo;s discuss exactly how we&rsquo;ll put the data in page
            design.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>Since at each checkpoint we choose to store only the number of flips that happened after the
            previous checkpoint, the </span><span class="c10">maximum number will be </span><span
            class="c10 c88">&radic;TotMoves</span><span class="c88">, </span><span class="c12">which is roughly
            1000.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>Storing an integer requires 4 bytes (or 32 bits), whereas we only need at maximum
        </span><span class="c10">10 bits</span><span>&nbsp;(2</span><span class="c39">10</span><span class="c12">&nbsp;=
            1024 &gt; 1000). Therefore, we assign each number of flips a fixed size of 10 bits. These bit strings can
            then be taken into sets of 8 bits and converted to character for storage (as we did with storing the moves
            in our original page design, in previous assignment).</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span>Let&rsquo;s say the page size allows storing </span><span class="c99">p</span><span
            class="c14">2</span><span>&nbsp;such flip numbers (or in other words, we can store </span><span
            class="c99">10p</span><span class="c14">2</span><span>&nbsp;bits in a page). Then we&rsquo;ll divide the
            whole board into subgrids of size </span><span class="c10 c99">ceil(N/p) </span><span class="c10">X
        </span><span class="c10 c99">ceil(N/p)</span><span class="c12">, allowing each sub-grid to be of a size that we
            can fit in a single page.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c21 c10">To optimise some queries (discussed later in the Queries section) even more,
            we&rsquo;ll be storing the total number of flips for each position throughout the game as well.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">Since this requires storing only one number for each position for a whole game
            (rather than for each checkpoint), this storage will be negligible (~0.1%) compared to the total storage
            we&rsquo;re using. Hence, we need not think a lot to optimise storage in this case and any way should work
            well.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c21 c10">Example:</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">For the sake of example, let&rsquo;s take a board of size 6X6, which will store
            checkpoints after every 6 moves.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c12"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c12">The game proceeds as follows:</span></p>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_61hph7qfzne-0 start" start="1">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span
                style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 208.43px; height: 209.50px;"><img
                    alt="" src="images/image20.png"
                    style="width: 208.43px; height: 209.50px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                    title=""></span><span class="c12">&nbsp;</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span
                style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 207.72px; height: 208.84px;"><img
                    alt="" src="images/image38.png"
                    style="width: 207.72px; height: 208.84px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"

        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span
                style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 208.99px; height: 210.17px;"><img

        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span
                style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 214.54px; height: 215.50px;"><img

        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span

        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span
                style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 215.41px; height: 216.17px;"><img
                    alt="" src="images/image19.png"
                    style="width: 215.41px; height: 216.17px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"

        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span
                style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 207.50px; height: 208.96px;"><img

                    title=""></span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span
                style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 204.96px; height: 205.85px;"><img

        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span

                    alt="" src="images/image35.png"
                    style="width: 217.50px; height: 218.62px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);"
                    title=""></span><span>&nbsp;</span><span class="c21 c10">CHECKPOINT</span></li>
    </ol>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c0">For the sake of simplicity, we don&rsquo;t show moves after 12.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c0">Now, the flips at the first checkpoint (after move 6) will be:</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p><a id="t.6f046d46223504cb0df051d23154940f3eea9d7a"></a><a

    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c4">We observe that till the first checkpoint, the cell </span><span
            class="c1 c10">(3,3)</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;(highlighted in green) flipped twice, once in move 3 and
            second time in move 6.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c0">Similarly we can find the flips for each cell at checkpoint 2 (after move 12) as
            well.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <hr>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <h2 class="c6" id="h.dizs7te8s8ry"><span class="c93 c10 c87 c4">Query 1 [LONGEVITY]</span></h2>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p><a id="t.a1405a792a88bbf48f7b8d7e34ec09be27ac2c16"></a><a
        id="t.14"></a>
    <table class="c44">
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c78" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c0">You are given a position (i,j) and the move on which you are currently
                        at. Then you need to answer the following: </span></p>
                <p class="c13 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
                <ol class="c8 lst-kix_n7thv5m855ee-0 start" start="1">
                    <li class="c13 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Whether the color at position (i,j) will be flipped
                            in the next move or not.</span></li>
                    <li class="c13 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">For how many moves you can guarantee that this
                            position will not be flipped.</span></li>
                    <li class="c13 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">In the next move, all positions in the board that
                            are going to become flippable.</span></li>
                </ol>
            </td>
        </tr>
    </table>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <h3 class="c24 c19 c18" id="h.alvxzviawd5m"><span class="c55 c10">Solving (a)</span></h3>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_1r93xvd4ejxj-0 start" start="1">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">We&rsquo;ll first find KNB using the current state of the
                game.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Proceed each of the KNB to 1 more step (we know the future of all
                those boards/games).</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">For each KNB, check if the position </span><span class="c1">(i,j)
            </span><span class="c0">flipped or not.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_1r93xvd4ejxj-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Empty cell -&gt; White =&gt; Flip</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Empty cell -&gt; Black =&gt; Flip</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">White -&gt; Black =&gt; Flip</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Black -&gt; White =&gt; Flip</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">In all the other cases =&gt; No Flip</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_1r93xvd4ejxj-0" start="4">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">There will be some boards saying that the given position will
                flip, and some will say not flipped, to decide the result </span><span class="c10 c4">take
                majority</span><span class="c0">.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_1r93xvd4ejxj-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">In case there is a tie (will only happen when </span><span
                class="c1">K</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;is even), </span><span class="c10 c4">we&rsquo;ll be
                pessimistic</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;and declare not flipped.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c0 c65">Time complexity (excluding the time taken to find KNB):</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_d6dv78ck1zgv-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">For each board, going to next step will take </span><span
                class="c1">O(N</span><span class="c1 c39">2</span><span class="c1">) </span><span class="c0">to simulate
                that move</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Total boards: number of nearest neighbours = </span><span
                class="c1">K</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Therefore, time complexity = </span><span
                class="c1">O(KN</span><span class="c1 c39">2</span><span class="c1">)</span></li>
    </ul>
    <h3 class="c19 c18 c24" id="h.2te1e5pmlhhj"><span class="c55 c10">Solving (b)</span></h3>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c0">In the proposed page design, at each checkpoint, for each cell we store the number of
            times the cell was flipped after the last checkpoint.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_qpfqpo2fzpy5-0 start" start="1">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Do steps 2 to 4 for each of the KNB:</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">We&rsquo;ll loop over all the checkpoints to find the first next
                checkpoint which has non-zero flips for position </span><span class="c1">(i,j)</span><span
                class="c0">.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">If, let&rsquo;s say, checkpoint </span><span
                class="c1">p</span><span class="c1 c15">i</span><span class="c4 c15">&nbsp;</span><span class="c4">has
                non-zero flips, then find the first move between </span><span class="c1">p</span><span
                class="c1 c15">i-1</span><span class="c4 c15">&nbsp;</span><span class="c4">and </span><span
                class="c1">p</span><span class="c1 c15">i </span><span class="c0">where the flip happened.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Now, the number of moves with no flips is all the moves between
                current move and </span><span class="c1">p</span><span class="c1 c15">i </span><span class="c4">+ moves
                between </span><span class="c1">p</span><span class="c1 c15">i </span><span class="c4">and </span><span
                class="c1">p</span><span class="c1 c15">i+1 </span><span class="c0">with no flips.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">To guarantee no flips, </span><span class="c10 c4">we&rsquo;ll be
                pessimistic and take the minimum of the results</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;given across all
                KNB.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c0 c91">Time complexity (excluding the time taken to find KNB):</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_yen1n5ddfg9r-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">For each board </span><span
                class="c1">O(&radic;TotMoves)</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;will be required to find the required
                checkpoint and then loop after that checkpoint to find the required move.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">In each iteration of loop (mentioned above), </span><span
                class="c1">O(N</span><span class="c1 c39">2</span><span class="c1">) </span><span class="c0">will be
                required to simulate that move.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">This will be done for </span><span class="c1">K</span><span
                class="c0">&nbsp;boards.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Therefore, time complexity = </span><span class="c1">O(K
                N</span><span class="c1 c39">2</span><span class="c1">&nbsp;&radic;TotMoves)</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c49 c10 c4">Alternate Approach</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_4jprb4wdbo72-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">An alternate approach would be to store the cumulative number of
                flips at each checkpoint (instead of storing only the change from the last checkpoint). This change can
                be made in PART 5 if implemented.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">This would result in reducing the time-complexity of finding the
                first next partition with the same number of flips (which now means that the change is 0) from
            </span><span class="c1">O(&radic;TotMoves) </span><span class="c4">to </span><span
                class="c52 c1">O(logTotMoves).</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">But, finding the exact move within the partition will still take
            </span><span class="c1">O(&radic;TotMoves)</span><span class="c0">, so the worst case in this alternate
                approach would still be the same as before.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <h3 class="c24 c19 c18" id="h.bd40dtcyplj2"><span class="c10 c55">Solving (c)</span></h3>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c0">This part is an enhanced version of part (a).</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_wvw55oafqz88-0 start" start="1">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">First find KNB using the current state of the game.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Advance each of the KNB to the next move.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">For each position </span><span class="c1">(i,j)</span><span
                class="c0">, follow the first 3 steps of part (a).</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">To decide whether position </span><span
                class="c1">(i,j)</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;becomes flippable or not, if it is flipped in any of the
                KNB, we&rsquo;ll say it is flippable, otherwise not.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c37 c41"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c91 c4">Time complexity</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;(after finding KNB):</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_9tkjbswnk5tq-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">For each board, going to next step will take </span><span
                class="c1">O(N</span><span class="c1 c39">2</span><span class="c1">) </span><span class="c0">to simulate
                that move</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Total boards: </span><span class="c1">K</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Therefore, time complexity = </span><span
                class="c1">O(KN</span><span class="c1 c39">2</span><span class="c1 c52">)</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c52 c1"></span></p>
    <hr>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c52 c1"></span></p>
    <h2 class="c6" id="h.vy9ihcvjchc9"><span class="c93 c10 c87 c4">Query 2 [DIFF IN FLIPS]</span></h2>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p><a id="t.02fa2e32bf53615bda4a4d0ff67c6a37db806690"></a><a
        id="t.15"></a>
    <table class="c44">
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c78" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c0">Suppose you are at the ith move and when player 1 plays (white) it turns
                        &ldquo;k&rdquo; blacks to white and subsequently when player 2 plays (black) it turns
                        &ldquo;l&rdquo; whites to black. Then we can define gain for player 1 as (k-l). Now, you need to
                        answer the following:</span></p>
                <p class="c13 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
                <ol class="c8 lst-kix_kff092u2o5yw-0 start" start="1">
                    <li class="c13 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Return all the i&rsquo;s such that player 1 is
                            gaining at least &ldquo;b&rdquo;</span></li>
                    <li class="c13 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Return all the sequences of moves (i,i+1,i+2, .....
                            i+p) such that player 1 is continuously gaining at least b in all these moves and p is the
                            highest such number.</span></li>
                </ol>
            </td>
        </tr>
    </table>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c4">For both the parts, we assume returning </span><span class="c1">i</span><span
            class="c0">&nbsp;means returning the move number.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c0">For the sake of simple explanation, we also assume that returning all means
            throughout the game, and not only from the current move number till the end of game. Even if the requirement
            is to return only future moves, the approach would be the same.</span></p>
    <h3 class="c24 c19 c18" id="h.s06syo846ltd"><span class="c55 c10">Solving (a)</span></h3>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_530pxzcjzn7j-0 start" start="1">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Find KNB according to the current state of the game.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Mark each move as positive (simply keep an array of size 1e6, in
                this case).</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">For each KNB, do steps from 4 to 6.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Go to each positive move one by one.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_530pxzcjzn7j-1 start" start="1">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">If the next positive move is in some later checkpoint, we can
                use the stored checkpoints to efficiently go to that state instead of incrementing moves one by
                one.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_530pxzcjzn7j-0" start="5">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Check if the player is gaining at least </span><span
                class="c1">b</span><span class="c0">:</span></li>
    </ol>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_530pxzcjzn7j-1 start" start="1">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">This would require checking the next two moves.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_530pxzcjzn7j-0" start="6">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">If the player gains less than </span><span
                class="c1">b</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;for some move number, mark that move as negative.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Return all the move numbers that are marked as positive.</span>
        </li>
    </ol>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c91 c4">Time complexity</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;(after finding KNB):</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_y6k81cvyc89c-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Looping over moves will require </span><span
                class="c1">O(TotMoves)</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">For each such move, simulating next two moves will require
            </span><span class="c1">O(N</span><span class="c1 c39">2</span><span class="c1">)</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">This needs to be done for </span><span class="c1">K</span><span
                class="c0">&nbsp;boards</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Therefore, time complexity = </span><span class="c1">O(K
                N</span><span class="c1 c39">2</span><span class="c1">&nbsp;TotMoves)</span></li>
    </ul>
    <h3 class="c24 c19 c18" id="h.cpicx2asvz63"><span class="c55 c10">Solving (b)</span></h3>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c0">This part is an extension of the above part.</span></p>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_pkbqts7mcwz7-0 start" start="1">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Find KNB according to the current state of the game.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Give each move a value of an infinite number, let&rsquo;s say,
                1e9 (simply keep an array of size 1e6, in this case).</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">For each KNB, do steps from 4 to 6.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Go to each move having value greater than 0</span></li>
    </ol>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_pkbqts7mcwz7-1 start" start="1">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">If the next required move is in some later checkpoint, we can
                use the stored checkpoints to efficiently go to that state instead of incrementing moves one by
                one.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_pkbqts7mcwz7-0" start="5">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">For each such move, find the maximum </span><span
                class="c1">p</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;such that at every move the player gains at least </span><span
                class="c1">b</span></li>
    </ol>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_pkbqts7mcwz7-1 start" start="1">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">This would require checking the next </span><span
                class="c1">p</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;moves.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">If we&rsquo;re doing it for consecutive moves, we can use the
                sliding window technique to optimise checking next </span><span class="c1">p</span><span
                class="c0">&nbsp;moves for all those consecutive moves.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_pkbqts7mcwz7-0" start="6">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Set the value of the move as minimum of the original value and
                the highest </span><span class="c1">p</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;we found in the above step.</span>
        </li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Return all </span><span class="c1">(i,p)</span><span
                class="c4">&nbsp;pairs (</span><span class="c1">i</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;is the move number, and
            </span><span class="c1">p</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;is the value stored for that move) where </span><span
                class="c1">p </span><span class="c0">is non-zero.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c37 c41"></span></p>
    <hr>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <h2 class="c6" id="h.b3hasbakq37l"><span class="c93 c10 c87 c4">Query 3 [MAX FLIPS]</span></h2>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p><a id="t.3a77f0b4286630bd1cb0abf3e7a9eec86ec6137c"></a><a
        id="t.16"></a>
    <table class="c44">
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c78" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c0">Return all locations (i,j) which suffered the maximum number of flips
                        which happened throughout the games played.</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
    </table>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c49 c10 c70"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c37 c41">In the proposed page design, we&rsquo;re storing the total number of flips
            for each game/board, and for each position.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c37 c41"></span></p>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_x1ocpkyq3f0e-0 start" start="1">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c37 c41">Find the KNB using the current state of the game.</span>
        </li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c70">For each position </span><span class="c40">(i,j)</span><span
                class="c37 c41">, have a counter, initialised with 0.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c70">Now for each KNB, for each position, increment the corresponding
                counter with the total number o</span><span class="c0">f flips of that position in that game.</span>
        </li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">To find the locations</span><span class="c37 c41">&nbsp;which
                suffered the maximum number of flips, take the position with the maximum value of the corresponding
                counter.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_x1ocpkyq3f0e-1 start" start="1">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c37 c41">In case of ties, return all such locations.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c37 c41"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c91 c70">Time complexity</span><span class="c37 c41">&nbsp;(after finding
            KNB):</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_mjfpn2os6b93-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c70">For each board, we need to get total number of flips for each
                cell which will require </span><span class="c40">O(N</span><span class="c40 c39">2</span><span
                class="c52 c40">)</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c70">This needs to be done for </span><span class="c40">K</span><span
                class="c37 c41">&nbsp;boards</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c70">Therefore, time-complexity = </span><span class="c40">O(K
                N</span><span class="c40 c39">2</span><span class="c40">)</span></li>
    </ul>
    <hr>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c37 c41"></span></p>
    <h2 class="c6" id="h.3kmyy7wnbaus"><span class="c93 c10 c87 c4">Query 4</span></h2><a
        id="t.a6478f5e7e08f6cbf49a747d8d3606510cfd5924"></a><a id="t.17"></a>
    <table class="c44">
        <tr class="c2">
            <td class="c78" colspan="1" rowspan="1">
                <p class="c13"><span class="c0">For the given board orientations, give me all the positions (i,j) which
                        will not change forever (based on the KNB) . That is No matter what you or the other player
                        plays the color at this position (i,j) will not change.</span></p>
            </td>
        </tr>
    </table>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c49 c10 c4">Case 1: Forever means from beginning to end</span></p>
    <p class="c5"><span class="c0">This case boils down to a slightly different version of Query 3.</span></p>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_io6i7i1iix0j-0 start" start="1">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Find the KNB using the current state of the game.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Keep all the positions </span><span class="c1">(i,j)</span><span
                class="c0">&nbsp;marked as not changed.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">For each of the KNB, for each position, if the total number of
                flips is more than one, then mark that position as changed.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_io6i7i1iix0j-1 start" start="1">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">We take more than one, because one flip is counted when turning
                an empty cell to black/white cell.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_io6i7i1iix0j-0" start="4">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Return all the positions marked as not changed.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <p class="c5 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c91 c4">Time complexity</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;(after finding KNB):</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_n9zdw33jydyi-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c70">For each board, we need to get total number of flips for each
                cell which will require </span><span class="c40">O(N</span><span class="c40 c39">2</span><span
                class="c52 c40">)</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c70">This needs to be done for </span><span class="c40">K</span><span
                class="c37 c41">&nbsp;boards</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c70">Therefore, time-complexity = </span><span class="c40">O(K
                N</span><span class="c40 c39">2</span><span class="c40">)</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c49 c10 c4">Case 2: Forever means from this (or the very next) move to the end</span>
    </p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_smsr48v3gvc9-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Very similar to the Case 1</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">In step 3, instead of taking the total number of flips,
                we&rsquo;ll need to take the number of flips after the current move.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_smsr48v3gvc9-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Since we&rsquo;re storing the number of flips at each
                checkpoint, we can compute this by looping over all the checkpoints.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c91 c4">Time complexity</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;(after finding KNB):</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_gjjhwh7nm1bz-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">For finding the number of flips in all future checkpoints,
            </span><span class="c1">O(&radic;TotMoves)</span><span class="c4">&nbsp;will be required, and </span><span
                class="c1">O(N</span><span class="c1 c39">2</span><span class="c1">&nbsp;&radic;TotMoves) </span><span
                class="c0">for simulating moves and finding flips in the current checkpoint.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">This needs to be done for </span><span class="c1">K</span><span
                class="c0">&nbsp;boards</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Therefore, time-complexity = </span><span class="c1">O(K
                N</span><span class="c1 c39">2</span><span class="c52 c1">&nbsp;&radic;TotMoves)</span></li>
    </ul>
    <hr>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <h2 class="c6" id="h.ql8baa4xu7ch"><span class="c93 c10 c87 c4">OPEN ENDED queries </span></h2>
    <h3 class="c24 c19 c18" id="h.a7kjztkedh4m"><span class="c55 c10">Other Query 1: Check if the current state is
            deterministic and the winning player is already decided</span></h3>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_lb4vz53reiwa-0 start" start="1">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Find KNB according to the current state of the game.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Store two counter variables, one for each of the players, both of
                them initialised to zero.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">For each board, we&rsquo;ll have the last state as one of the
                checkpoints, so simply check that to decide if the required player won or not.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Depending on which player won, increment the corresponding
                counter.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">If either of the counters is still zero, return that the game is
                at a deterministic state.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c91 c4">Time complexity </span><span class="c0">(after finding KNB):</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_hn8nutcbv4po-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">To check the winning player of each board, </span><span
                class="c1">O(N</span><span class="c1 c39">2</span><span class="c1">) </span><span class="c0">will be
                required.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">This needs to be done for </span><span class="c1">K</span><span
                class="c0">&nbsp;boards.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Therefore, time-complexity = </span><span class="c1">O(K
                N</span><span class="c1 c39">2</span><span class="c52 c1">)</span></li>
    </ul>
    <h3 class="c24 c19 c18" id="h.i88jqv46dw8u"><span class="c55 c10">Other Query 2: Check the maximum flips possible in
            the next move according to KNB. This will allow the player to aim somewhere near that value while taking a
            move.</span></h3>
    <ol class="c8 lst-kix_k660su5v77sz-0 start" start="1">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Find KNB according to the current state of the game.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Proceed each board to the next move and find the number of
                flips.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Return the maximum number of flips possible over all the
            </span><span class="c1">K </span><span class="c0">boards.</span></li>
    </ol>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c91 c4">Time complexity</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;(after finding KNB):</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_lmvhg88cxeek-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">To proceed to the next move and find the number of flips
            </span><span class="c1">O(N</span><span class="c1 c39">2</span><span class="c1">) </span><span
                class="c0">will be required.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">This needs to be done for </span><span class="c1">K</span><span
                class="c0">&nbsp;boards.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">Therefore, time-complexity = </span><span class="c1">O(K
                N</span><span class="c1 c39">2</span><span class="c1">)</span></li>
    </ul>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0 c20"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18"><span class="c10 c4">KEY TAKEAWAYS</span></p>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_ow9yr0ir4rsa-0 start">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">There is always a tradeoff between utilisation of time and space
                based resources.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Query optimization, index optimization, and schema optimization
                go hand in hand.</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c4">For query execution, though we did not have any logical AND\OR
                operations, in order for efficiently executing the</span><span class="c10 c4">&nbsp;&ldquo;K Nearest
                Neighbours&rdquo;</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;query, we effectively use several optimizations
                like:</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_ow9yr0ir4rsa-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10 c4">Secondary index</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;for Voronoi
                Tessellation in Part 0</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c10 c4">Extendible hashing</span><span class="c0">&nbsp;for our
                Jaccard based similarity metric</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_ow9yr0ir4rsa-0">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">New page design for executing queries: query 1b, query 3 and
                query 4</span></li>
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Sometimes, there maybe &nbsp;overlap in the operations involved
                in query execution for 2 queries</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_ow9yr0ir4rsa-1 start">
        <li class="c5 c11 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">For eg: we use the result query 1a in implementing the retrieval
                for query(1c) as well.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <ul class="c8 lst-kix_ow9yr0ir4rsa-0">
        <li class="c5 c7 li-bullet-0"><span class="c0">Our page design and indexing mechanism depended on our query
                execution algorithm.</span></li>
    </ul>
    <hr>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
    <p class="c5 c18 c17"><span class="c0"></span></p>
